# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

60-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of Prometheus metric registration patterns across the three repositories. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I analyzed how Prometheus metrics are registered and exposed in **kubernetes/kubernetes**, **grafana/grafana**, and **prometheus/prometheus**, identifying three distinct architectural approaches:

### **Kubernetes** - Custom KubeRegistry Wrapper
- Implements a sophisticated abstraction layer in `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/registry.go`
- Wraps the native Prometheus registry with additional capabilities (metric versioning, deprecation tracking, stability levels)
- Uses a global `legacyregistry` module for centralized registration
- Metrics registered via `legacyregistry.MustRegister()` using `sync.Once` guards

### **Prometheus** - Direct Native Registry
- Uses standard Prometheus client library without wrappers
- Metrics created directly via `prometheus.NewCounter()`, `prometheus.NewGauge()`, etc.
- Registration happens via `prometheus.MustRegister()` at init time or through registerer parameters
- Examples: `template/template.go`, `scrape/metrics.go`, `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`

### **Grafana** - promauto Automatic Registration
- Uses modern `promauto.With(registerer)` for automatic metric registration
- Most concise approach with metrics created and registered in one step
- Metrics organized in struct types within functions like `NewSchedulerMetrics()`
- Examples: `pkg/services/ngalert/metrics/scheduler.go`, `pkg/infra/metrics/metrics.go`

The analysis includes **25 key files** and **16 important symbols** across all three repositories with detailed explanations in `/workspace/answer.json`.

across the three repositories, reflecting their distinct architectural approaches:\\n\\n## Kubernetes/kubernetes - Custom KubeRegistry Wrapper\\n\\nKubernetes implements a sophisticated abstraction layer wrapping the Prometheus registry. The core is in `staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/registry.go`, which defines a custom `KubeRegistry` interface that wraps `prometheus.Registry`. This wrapper provides additional capabilities including:\\n\\n- Metric deprecation lifecycle management (StabilityLevel markers: ALPHA, BETA, STABLE)\\n- Version-aware metric visibility (metrics can be hidden based on Kubernetes version)\\n- Custom collectors via `StableCollector` interface\\n- Meta-metrics tracking total registered/disabled/hidden metrics\\n\\nA global `legacyregistry` module (`staging/src/k8s.io/component-base/metrics/legacyregistry/registry.go`) provides module-level registration functions like `MustRegister()` and `RawMustRegister()`. Metrics are defined throughout the codebase (e.g., `pkg/kubelet/metrics/metrics.go`, `pkg/scheduler/metrics/metrics.go`, `pkg/proxy/metrics/metrics.go`) using Kubernetes-specific metric constructors and are registered via `legacyregistry.MustRegister()` in sync.Once-protected functions to ensure single registration.\\n\\n## Prometheus/prometheus - Direct Native Registry\\n\\nPrometheus uses the standard Prometheus client library registry directly without wrapper abstractions. Metrics are created and registered via:\\n\\n1. **Init-time registration**: Global metrics defined in var blocks are registered in init() functions using `prometheus.MustRegister()` (e.g., `template/template.go` with `templateTextExpansionFailures` and `templateTextExpansionTotal`)\\n\\n2. **Function-based registration**: Many components encapsulate metrics in structs with a constructor function that takes a `prometheus.Registerer` parameter. For example, `scrape/metrics.go` defines `scrapeMetrics` struct with individual prometheus.Counter, prometheus.Gauge, and prometheus.Histogram fields that are instantiated in `newScrapeMetrics(reg prometheus.Registerer)` and registered via `reg.Register()` calls within error handling blocks.\\n\\n3. **Lazy registration**: Components like `storage/remote/queue_manager.go` define `queueManagerMetrics` and register metrics when needed using `reg.MustRegister()`\\n\\nThis approach keeps registration coupled with business logic and provides maximum flexibility for different initialization patterns across the codebase.\\n\\n## Grafana/grafana - promauto Automatic Registration\\n\\nGrafana uses the modern `promauto` library for automatic metric registration. The pattern is:\\n\\n1. **Registerer-based construction**: Metrics are created in functions taking `prometheus.Registerer` parameter (e.g., `NewSchedulerMetrics(r prometheus.Registerer)` in `pkg/services/ngalert/metrics/scheduler.go`)\\n\\n2. **Automatic registration via promauto**: Instead of manual registration, metrics are created with `promauto.With(r).NewCounter()`, `promauto.With(r).NewGauge()`, `promauto.With(r).NewHistogram()` which automatically registers them with the provided registerer\\n\\n3. **Struct-based metric grouping**: Related metrics are organized in structs (Scheduler, NotificationHistorian, RemoteAlertmanager) stored as fields, allowing cohesive metric lifecycle management\\n\\nExamples include `pkg/infra/metrics/metrics.go` (core metrics), `pkg/registry/apis/provisioning/jobs/metrics.go`, `pkg/services/ngalert/metrics/scheduler.go` (which uses promauto with Namespace and Subsystem organization), and `pkg/storage/unified/resource/bleve_index_metrics.go` (using native histogram buckets).\\n\\nGrafana's approach is most modern and declarative, with automatic registration reducing boilerplate and making the metric definition more concise than explicit registration calls.\"\n}\n",
